Important News

Central Political Conference 70

221st Meeting The Central Political Conference held its 221st meeting at 9:00 AM today (2nd). The attending committee members were Lin Sen, Tan Yankai, Wang Chonghui, Gu Yingfen, Hu Hanmin, He Yingqin, and Sun Ke. The attending observers were Chen Lifu, Li Wenfan, Kong Xiangxi, and Liu Jiwen. The chairman was Tan Yankai. The matters discussed were as follows: (1) Report from the Legal Group, reviewing the case transferred from the Central Executive Committee by the Zhejiang Provincial Executive Committee requesting the abolition of the deprivation of civil rights for bankrupt individuals. After investigating, the deprivation of civil rights is a type of accessory punishment. If there is no principal punishment, then the accessory punishment cannot exist. Therefore, simple bankruptcy without criminal issues will not lead to the deprivation of civil rights. The original case's concerns should be noted when drafting the bankruptcy law. Whether this is appropriate is still awaiting public decision. Decision: referred to the Legislative Yuan. (2) Report from the Legal Group, reviewing the case transferred from the Central Executive Committee by the Qingdao Special Municipality Party Affairs Guidance Committee requesting amendments to the law on the surrender of Communists. The request is to amend Article 7 of the law on the surrender of Communists to read "Surrender should be approved by a high-ranking party department before being made to the court or other government office." This is because they believe that high-ranking party departments are more accurate and knowledgeable in assessing the validity of a Communist's surrender than courts or other government offices. This is out of prudence and thoroughness and seems acceptable. Whether this is appropriate is still awaiting public decision. Decision: referred to the Legislative Yuan. (3) Report from the Ministry of Education regarding compliance with the resolution of the Second Plenary Session of the Third Central Executive Committee to organize a committee for drafting educational plans, compile a national education improvement plan, and submit it to the National Education Conference for discussion. A paper for instruction is respectfully presented for approval. Decision: referred to the Education Group for review.

Han's Troops Pass Near Xuzhou 71

Han's Military Relocation Has Been Completed

Xuzhou Correspondence Han Fuju was originally scheduled to leave for Jinan on the evening of the 30th. However, after learning that Ma Hongkui had arrived in Xuzhou from Jinan, he did not leave and remained at the Huayuan Hotel. Most of the accompanying personnel still stayed on the train. Mr. Haitao, who travels back and forth between Beijing and Kaifeng, also stayed at the same hotel. The reporter recently visited Mr. Haitao, who said that Commander Ma came to Xuzhou because he heard that Commander Han was in Xuzhou and needed to meet with Commander Liu. There were no other important matters. Commander Ma's special train arrived at the Xuzhou station at 4:00 AM today (31st). Commander Ma got out of the train and entered the city at about 5:00 AM and met with Commander Han at the Huayuan Hotel. He then went to headquarters to meet with Liu Zhi. It is heard that Han has been newly appointed as the Commander-in-Chief of the Communist Suppression in Hebei, Shandong, Henan, and has sent his secretary Zhang Shaotang to Beijing to meet with Chiang Kai-shek to report on the military relocation. He has also set up an office in Xuzhou to facilitate liaison, appointing Tian Wenzhong as the director and Chen Xibo as the deputy. As for Ma, it is heard that he has recently been ordered by Chiang Kai-shek to be responsible for handling the aftermath of Gao Guizi's remnants.

Regarding the relocation of Han's troops, according to recent news from the railway, the relocation of Han's troops has been completed. Armored trains with numbers such as Shandong Taishan and Beiping served as rear guards, with two infantry brigades flanking both sides of the railway line, slowly marching forward. Zhang Tingxian, captain of the Taishan armored train team, led his team to Xuzhou this morning. Zhao Jinshan, captain of the Beiping armored train team, led his team to Xuzhou this afternoon. Both were transferred to Yanzhou and then to Jining. The Shandong armored train is still patrolling around Liuhe Guide. The troops of Han's army marching on foot from eastern Henan to western Shandong are still in transit. It is heard that the vanguard of Wan Xuancai has passed Kaifeng and arrived at Luowang.

During this relocation of Han's troops, the main part and the supplies passing through Xuzhou consisted of more than a dozen trains. Adjutant Cao Xingzan, Transportation Commander Chen Guixin, and Military Grain Bureau Chief Mo Runtian all led their subordinates, military hospitals, and military supplies, causing very crowded transportation. By today, the military transport of Han's troops passing through Xuzhou has been completed. (March 31st)

Liu Xiang Purchases Large Numbers of Aircraft 72

Seven Bombers En Route

Chongqing Correspondence For the past two years, Liu Xiang has been actively expanding his military force and establishing an air force. Last time, the army accidentally killed and injured more than 100 military officers during a test launch of aircraft bombs. However, these two aircraft are not the largest, strongest, or most powerful equipment of the army. There are still seven large aircraft that have not yet arrived. Now, Guiyang and Hankou have sent telegrams stating that they are expected to arrive in Chongqing one after another in about a week. Originally, the army purchased nine aircraft. Three were purchased from Paris, and four were produced in Germany, contracted by a foreign company in Shanghai, and transported to Sichuan from Shanghai. They have now arrived in Hankou. As for the two aircraft that were test-flown at Guangyangba last time, they were manufactured in the United States and were the latest type of training aircraft, each worth 14,000 yuan and 90 horsepower each. The aircraft purchased in Germany and France are reconnaissance, fighter, and bomber aircraft, which can be used for aerial machine gun firing. They are larger than the two purchased in the United States, with a value ranging from 30,000 to 50,000. The German aircraft are the largest, with 372 horsepower and a value of 75,000 yuan. All aircraft are en route and should arrive in Chongqing soon. It is heard that Liu has hired a German aircraft instructor to open an aircraft training school, selecting 60 officers from the company, platoon, and squad levels to train as pilots. Classes will start soon. (China News Agency)

Guangzhou Agricultural Products Inspection Office 73

Implementing Inspection of Agricultural Product Pests and Diseases

Officially Opens on April 1st

Guangzhou Dispatch: The Guangzhou Agricultural Products Inspection Office, established by order of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, has been handling the inspection of agricultural products in Guangdong, Guangxi, Fujian, Yunnan, and other provinces. It has been conducting phased inspections of agricultural product raw materials, plant and animal pests and diseases, and fertilizers, based on the "Agricultural Product Inspection Regulations" promulgated by the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining. The fertilizer inspection has been in operation for several months, and the inspection procedures are quite thorough. Consequently, the counterfeit and substandard fertilizers being imported have been increasingly eradicated, benefiting farmers invisibly. The office recognizes that coastal Fujian and Guangdong have extensive international connections. Every year, a large number of plant seeds, seedlings, fruits, and aquatic products are imported and exported. This international movement of goods often serves as a medium for the spread of plant and animal pests and diseases. Examples include potato canker disease from the US to England, grape downy mildew from the US to France, citrus canker disease from Asia to the US, hibiscus scale insects from Japan to the US, and anthrax of livestock from Russia to Japan. The annual losses amount to tens of millions of dollars. It is estimated that the value of agricultural products imported into our country each year is over 700 million customs taels, according to statistics from 1929. In reality, many pests and diseases inevitably reside within them. For instance, China did not have rinderpest in ancient times, but it is now prevalent everywhere, causing severe damage and huge losses to farmers. The origin of this pathogen is believed to be from Europe. The introduction of other pests and diseases is also a cause for concern. For example, the Mexican boll weevil is extremely harmful to cotton production in the United States, and the annual import of American cotton into our country reaches about 200,000 dan (a unit of weight). The opportunity for this insect to be introduced is self-evident. Furthermore, many kinds of pathogens and pests, in their original habitats, are not very harmful due to the constraints of climate and natural enemies, or the strong resistance of the host. Once they are transferred to a different location, they lose their balance and can cause major disasters, as exemplified by the grape phylloxera imported from America to France. Therefore, advanced countries in the East and West, recognizing the danger of the spread of agricultural product pests and diseases, have established specialized agencies to inspect agricultural products for export and import, according to legal procedures, before they are allowed to be transported, to prevent problems before they occur. Our country's exported agricultural products often have attached pathogens and pests. They are either tragically burned or required to pay heavy ransoms for fumigation before they can be imported. As a result, some merchants, for convenience, transport agricultural products to Yokohama, where the Japanese inspection office performs inspections and issues certificates before they are transported to Honolulu, San Francisco, Seattle, and other places for sale. Furthermore, in January 1925, the Dutch government notified the former Beijing Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that from July 1st of the same year, all agricultural products transported from China to Dutch territories must be certified by a responsible agency as being free of dangerous pests and diseases before they are allowed to be imported. However, the former foreign affairs authorities shelved the matter and did not address it. Since then, our country's agricultural products have been unable to enter Dutch territory, resulting in countless losses over the years. In order to guarantee the credit of exported agricultural products and prevent the spread of imported pests and diseases, the office, in accordance with the methods of various countries, submitted a request to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining to add an agricultural product inspection department to handle pest and disease inspection matters. The Ministry has approved the request and will initially inspect four types of products: seeds, seedlings, fruits, and aquatic products. Branch offices will be established in Xiamen, Fuzhou, Shantou, and other places to handle fertilizer and pest and disease inspections, in the hope that plant and animal pests and diseases can be gradually eradicated, and to recover domestic and international losses. It is reported that the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining has dispatched Zhang Jingou to Guangdong to preside over the implementation. Other inspection personnel have also been appointed separately. Preparations are now complete, and the office is scheduled to officially open on April 1st. (March 27th)

Reconstruction Plan for the Huanghuagang Martyrs Cemetery 74

The Entire Project is Divided into Three Phases

Guangzhou Dispatch: The Guangdong Provincial Government and the Revolutionary Memorial Society have recently determined that the Huanghuagang Seventy-Two Martyrs Cemetery has been neglected for a long time, and various buildings have been added arbitrarily without a concrete plan, while the construction projects that should have been carried out have not been implemented. It has been decided to add a Seventy-Two Martyrs Photo Gallery and inscriptions in the cemetery. The Provincial Government has hired Lin Yun'gai, Lin Zhimian, Hu Yisheng, and Deng Yanhua to oversee the engineering surveys and planning. Recently, Lin Yun'gai and others have submitted a "Building Opinion on Reconstructing Huanghuagang" to the Provincial Government, based on their survey results. The content roughly states that the Huanghuagang Seventy-Two Martyrs Cemetery should be in the style of a cemetery, not a park. The current plans for tea pavilions, pools, etc., greatly detract from the solemnity of a cemetery. This is something that architecture should pay attention to. The buildings and all the arrangements in Huanghuagang should aim for solemnity and grandeur, so that later generations who come to this place will feel respect and awe. It should not give people the feeling of being in a garden or playground. Therefore, colorful wine shops, mahjong parlors, and tea pavilions should not be added to avoid creating a sense of irreverence. The proposed reconstruction is roughly divided into three phases. In the first phase, the most economical and easiest to implement changes will be made first. (1) The small and pointed stele in the middle of the martyrs' graves should be removed, and a Chinese-style stele should be erected in front of it, with the words "Tomb of the Seventy-Two Martyrs" written on it. The tomb should be built into an ancient steamed bun shape and planted with green grass. The location of the martyrs' memorial碑 is most suitable in the骆墓 area, because that place is high and open, making it easy to attract attention from near and far. (2) The existing music stage is not in the style of a music stage, and the inscription "Sharing Joy with All" is very inappropriate. It would be a laughing stock for generations to make music and seek pleasure in front of the tomb. It should be removed immediately, and there is no need to establish a music stage. (3) The inscription pavilion is too inferior and should also be removed (the stone tablet will be relocated separately). (4) Near the music pavilion is the tomb marker of General Yu, which looks like a stele pavilion or a paper burner. It is ugly and unsightly and should be removed. The tomb marker should be moved to the Revolutionary Memorial Hall for display, because none of the seventy-two martyrs have tomb markers, and it is too unique for General Yu alone to have one. (5) Plant old cypress trees on both sides of the main road and on both sides of the branch roads to create a solemn atmosphere. Seasonal flowers can be displayed on the grass on the right side of the tomb, but should not be arbitrarily displayed in front of the tomb. (6) The cemetery and the large grassland on the right should be planted with ancient pine and red cotton trees to show that they are connected to the cemetery but separated by the meaning. (7) The stone incense burner pillars are too dilapidated and should be removed. (8) Now that the boundary line of the cemetery has been clearly defined and is dedicated to the tomb of the seventy-two martyrs, how can other steles and tombs be allowed to be mixed in? Tombs such as the 骆墓, Du Shunchang tomb, and Shi tomb should all be moved out of the cemetery of the seventy-two martyrs to show respect. (9) The red house on the left side of the memorial archway is an irregular shape compared to the memorial archway and should be removed. (10) The Statue of Liberty in the memorial field is an idol worshiped by people from other countries. The tomb of the seventy-two martyrs is set up to worship the Chinese revolutionary martyrs. Placing the Statue of Liberty in the cemetery is tantamount to letting a foreigner live in supreme honor and surpass the seventy-two martyrs, which is a big mistake. If you want to take back the meaning of our freedom, you can move the Statue of Liberty to a suitable location and just use it as decoration, but the technology is too bad. (11) The location of the pool is not level with the road in front of the tomb, and it has no special meaning in terms of art. For the sake of temporary convenience, it should be changed to a round shape to enhance the grandeur, and special attention should be paid to the decoration of the pool in terms of Chinese and foreign art. Second Phase: (1) Acquire the fields under the moon platform in front of the tomb to build roads, dismantle the existing moon platform, and connect it to the main road in the front, leading directly to Dongsha Road. It would be best to acquire all the land on both sides of the road, along Dongsha Road to the east to the edge of the hill and to the west to the intersection of the existing archway. If not much can be done, at least one hundred feet should be acquired on both sides of the road. Moreover, there is a lot of unused land in the northwest corner of the cemetery, which can be exchanged for the land planned to be acquired in front. When the tomb has been changed into an ancient steamed bun shape, a new ancient-style stele will be built and erected in front of the tomb, with the seven big characters "Tomb of the Seventy-Two Martyrs" inscribed on it. (2) At the entrance of the main road from Dongsha Road, build a magnificent and simple archway, with Mr. Sun's inscription "Great Spirit Lives Forever" embedded in it, which will be the main entrance. The existing main entrance will be changed to a side door. (3) The four characters "Great Spirit Lives Forever" inscribed by the Premier on the memorial archway at the back should be re-engraved on the front archway to make it look grand and solemn. The four characters should be combined into one to make it look generous. The inscription should be in one line and should not be messed up, so that it can be seen from near and far and arouse memories and respect. (4) When there are sufficient funds, the branch roads on both sides should be widened appropriately. Third Phase: (1) Projects that are too grand. (2) Projects that are too difficult to finance. (3) Projects that take too long. (4) Projects that have not yet attracted the attention of most people. (5) Other matters will be included in the third phase. In order to temporarily save trouble, they are not explained in detail. It is best to set up another committee to temporarily manage the above plan. After the management is completed, it will be handed over to the Revolutionary Memorial Society for management. (March 28th)

Crisis of the Northeast Railways 75

Debt Status of the Siping-Taonan, Taonan-Ang'angxi, Jilin-Changchun, and Jilin-Dunhua Railways

Shenyang Dispatch: The Northeast region has a network of railways that is among the best in the country. However, its debt is deep and its operations are losing money. A thorough investigation reveals a situation that is truly chilling. Currently, with the exception of the Shenhai, Huhuai, and Jihai Railways, the Bei'ning Railway has borrowed British funds, and its operations can still be maintained. However, the Siping-Taonan, Taonan-Ang'angxi, Jilin-Changchun, and Jilin-Dunhua Railways, which have borrowed Japanese funds, are all nominally built with borrowed funds, but the methods of borrowing are different. The Jilin-Changchun Railway entrusted the management to an agent, the Siping-Taonan Railway issued bonds, and the Jilin-Dunhua and Taonan-Ang'angxi Railways contracted the construction projects. If the conditions were appropriate and they were properly utilized, it would not be impossible to use them for development. However, these four railways failed to utilize foreign capital and were instead utilized by foreign capital. They were exploited and eroded and are on the verge of death, which is truly lamentable. The Northeast Communications Committee previously convened a communications conference to try to find a quick solution, but based on the current situation of each railway, it is feared that it will be difficult to remedy the situation. The operational debt situation of the Siping-Taonan, Taonan-Ang'angxi, Jilin-Changchun, and Jilin-Dunhua Railways is investigated as follows:

Debt Amount

(1) Siping-Taonan Railway: When building the Siping-Zhengjiatun line in 1915, it borrowed 5 million Japanese yen from the Yokohama Specie Bank. The term of the loan was set at 40 years. The important conditions were that during the term of the loan, the chief engineer, traffic manager, and chief accountant of the railway must be Japanese. The interest rate on the loan was 5% per annum. When it was extended to Siping-Taonan in 1920, it continued to borrow, for a total of 45 million yen. A new Siping-Taonan loan contract was signed, which included the original 5 million yen borrowed for Siping-Zhengjiatun. At that time, the Yokohama Specie Bank's claim was completely transferred to the South Manchuria Railway Company. After the contract was established, the South Manchuria Railway Company was also unable to handle the large amount of money and tried to raise funds in major European and American markets. Due to the European War, it was unable to do so. It had no choice but to revise the contract into a short-term contract of 10 million yen, with the same conditions as before, but the annual interest rate was increased to 9%, and it was compound interest. As of the end of May 1925, the railway's debt had reached 32 million yen. At that time, the railway director dared not continue to sign a rollover contract and repeatedly negotiated with the creditor to reduce the interest rate, but it was futile. From June 1925 to the end of December of last year, the railway's loan interest had accumulated to more than 15 million Japanese yen. The total of principal and interest was more than 52 million Japanese yen. (2) Taonan-Ang'angxi Railway: The Taonan-Ang'angxi loan was made by signing a contract with the South Manchuria Railway Company to contract the construction project. The total estimated cost of the entire railway project was 12.92 million yen. The main condition was that the railway should hire a Japanese consultant, whose powers were incomparable to those of consultants in various Chinese agencies. He could represent the South Manchuria Railway Company and have overall administrative power over the railway. The advance payment budget was itemized, but when the final accounts were submitted, the South Manchuria Railway Company suddenly added 2 million yen for various expenses (various expenses including entertainment expenses, or possibly movement expenses, are also unknown). The purpose of these various expenses was purely for purposes outside the railway before the construction project was contracted, so they could not be included in the advance payment. The railway bureau initially requested a reduction, but then denied it altogether, saying that the expenses had not been submitted to the province. The South Manchuria Railway Company not only refused to cancel it, but also did not express any intention of reducing it. Negotiations are still ongoing. In addition, there are three other things that are worth noting: 1. The South Manchuria Railway Company advanced more than 2.36 million Japanese yen for the purchase of vehicles, with interest accruing from December 17, 1928, at an interest rate of 9%. 2. Short-term loan for fuel and coal prices was more than 800,000 Japanese yen, which was added to the principal and calculated as compound interest (the railway's coal was purchased from Japanese factories, with a price of 17 yen per ton, which is about double the price of domestic goods. This may be limited by the contract relationship, and there is nothing that can be done about it). 3. The Liaoning Provincial Government previously borrowed 2 million Japanese yen from the railway at an annual interest rate of 9%, which has not yet been repaid. The railway's bridge construction fee refers to this loan. If it is not repaid, it will inevitably be added to the principal and calculated as compound interest. In total, the railway has borrowed more than 20.79 million Japanese yen in total before and after. (3) Jilin-Dunhua Railway: The original loan for the railway was 18 million Japanese yen, and then another 6 million Japanese yen was added, for a total of 24 million Japanese yen. It was also invested by the South Manchuria Railway Company and a construction contract was signed. The interest rate was also between 9%. The main condition was to hire a Japanese chief engineer, whose powers were the same as the consultant of the Taonan-Ang'angxi Railway, but the engineering was shoddy and almost unusable. The biggest problem is the railway's project acceptance. According to the report of the project acceptance committee sent by the Transportation Committee, the total project cost was at most more than 13 million Japanese yen, while the railway's accounts show more than 26 million Japanese yen (including interest). It is reported that the railway project had just been completed and had not been investigated, but the chairman of the railway project acceptance committee replied to the acceptance. (The chairman of the committee is Mr. So-and-so, the supervisory section chief of the railway, who is from Lishu County and graduated from a certain middle school and has a marriage relationship with the railway director.) The Transportation Committee is now thoroughly investigating this matter. (4) Jilin-Changchun Railway: The original loan for the railway was 2.5 million Japanese yen. In 1918, another 4 million Japanese yen was borrowed from the South Manchuria Railway Company, for a total of 6.5 million Japanese yen, with an annual interest rate of 5% and a term of 30 years. The fatal condition was that during the term of the loan, the railway was entrusted to the South Manchuria Railway Company to be managed. The railway bureau purchased 80-pound steel rails, and the South Manchuria Railway Company advanced 1 million Japanese yen, with an annual compound interest rate of 9%. The steel rails were purely old materials and did not comply with the approved original plan. It was also agreed with the South Manchuria Railway Company that interest should be calculated twice a year before a formal loan contract was signed and added to the principal for compound interest. The aforementioned interest totaled more than 80,000 Japanese yen as of the end of 1928, and the interest for 1929 is not included. In total, the railway has a debt of more than 8.91 million Japanese yen before and after.

Operational Status 76

(1) Siping-Taonan: In 1928, the railway's operating revenue was more than 6.06 million yuan, operating expenses were more than 3.61 million yuan, and the interest payable on loans was more than 5.42 million yuan. After offsetting revenue and expenditure, there was a shortfall of more than 2.97 million yuan. (2) Taonan-Ang'angxi: In 1928, the railway's operating revenue was more than 2.2 million yuan, operating expenses were more than 1.9 million yuan, and the interest payable on various advances was more than 2.24 million yuan. After offsetting revenue and expenditure, there was a shortfall of more than 1.92 million yuan. (3) Jilin-Changchun: In 1928, the railway's operating revenue was more than 3.62 million yuan, operating expenses were more than 2.55 million yuan, and the interest payable on loans was more than 660,000 yuan. After offsetting revenue and expenditure, there was a surplus of 40,000 yuan. (4) Jilin-Dunhua: The railway opened for business in the second half of 1928. The revenue and expenditure situation has not yet been calculated. However, the area is remote and the railway is just beginning operations. Both passenger and freight transportation are far less prosperous than the above railways. It can be asserted that there will be no huge revenue, and the more than 2.81 million yuan of interest payable on advances each year is an unavoidable expense. In total, the income of the above four railways, except for the Jilin-Changchun Railway, which has less loan interest and can still cope, the total income of the rest is only enough to cover the interest, or even not enough to cover the interest, and the compound interest is increasing without end. In the future, the total debt will become progressively larger, which is truly the crisis of the Northeast Railways. (March 25th)

Second Trial of the Gao Ying Appeal Case (Continued) 77

Further Interrogation of Gao Ying

Judge: Did you say that the consulate did not have the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' seals?

Answer: Yes.

Judge: Then where did the seals on your luggage come from?

Answer: If they are not fake, then they were obtained from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. I think they were probably obtained from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Judge: Have you ever obtained them?

Answer: I have never obtained them.

Judge: Then you should know that these seals were obtained from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs?

Answer: If they were not obtained from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, then they were privately made.

Judge: It is not surprising to privately make seals. It is even easier to privately make documents. But are the seals on your luggage from the consulate?

Answer: The consulate has never obtained seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, so these seals were definitely not issued by our consulate.

Judge: Do you know Shen Guang and the other four people?

Answer: No.

Judge: These people have already been investigated by the Guangdong High Court. Now we have a reply stating that they have no dealings with the Hong Kong and Guangdong Bank. Now, please take a look at this letter. (Shows the reply for review) You all said that you don't know the addresses of these people. Our court has specifically investigated the Hong Kong and Guangdong Bank for the sake of prudence. (After reading the letter, Gao Ying returned the original to the judge without answering)

Judge: Chen Sheng lives on North Sichuan Road in Shanghai, but we have investigated and cannot find him. Do you know where he lives on North Sichuan Road?

Answer: I went to the United States in 1925, so I don't know.

Finally, Gao Ying requested to make the following points: (1) Regarding the seals, the seals are from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, not the consulate. Therefore, the Jiangning District Court's judgment that the seals are from the consulate is not valid. Moreover, of the fourteen pieces of luggage, three of my own did not have seals, and only the eleven pieces entrusted by Chen Sheng had seals. (3) The Jiangning District Court's judgment that I went to the pier to greet and take care of the luggage is also not true. I went to the pier to pick up my wife and did not take care of other things. (3) The judgment stated that when I detained the boxes at the customs, I telegraphed Minister Wu, claiming that there were a small amount of drugs in the boxes, which my wife had brought under someone else's influence, and requested assistance. The word "influence" is a mistranslation of the telegram code. It should be the word "deceived." At that time, I asked Mr. Huamo, the tax officer of the customs, and he said that according to the report of Harris and Smeth, the drug section members of the customs detective department, there were drugs in the boxes, and that was when I found out.

Judge: The judgment also stated that I firmly refused to announce the names of the people who contacted and transported Ya opium in China and San Francisco, etc., which was also a report made by Consul General Gong to Minister Wu because of a disagreement between Consul General Gong and me. When Gao Ying stated this, Lawyer Liu Shifang presented a letter from Lawyer Walter Lair, the legal advisor of the Chinese Consulate in San Francisco, proving that Consul General Gong and Gao Ying had disagreements. Please pay attention to the court. At that time, he presented the letter for review. After reading it, the judge returned it. Gao Ying replied that the above points should be carefully investigated by the court to clarify the truth. It was already past three o'clock. The clerk stood up to read the confession and ordered Gao Ying, Gao Liao, and Sun Yuan to sign separately. The judge announced that the case would be further investigated by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and that a retrial would be scheduled. The court was adjourned.

Appendix: Letter from Lawyer Walter Lair of San Francisco to Lawyer Liu Shifang

Dear Sir:

I have received your letter of January 16 regarding the Gao Ying case. I am very willing to assist Mr. Gao as you mentioned in your letter. However, due to my position, it would not only be detrimental to my duties, but also very difficult. Because I am still the legal advisor of the Consulate of former Consul General Gong and have not yet reached the end of my term. In addition, there are Mr. Gong's property and other matters (Mr. Gong currently holds a power of attorney). Before Mr. Gong leaves the United States to return to China, I will complete the cleanup for him. Therefore, if I make any statements about Mr. Gong, it will be presented to the Chinese court as evidence, and the Chinese newspapers here will reprint it. It is extremely difficult for me to publish my business and legal affairs as Mr. Gong's lawyer and draw attention from all parties. I hope you will forgive me for this situation. It is well known that Mr. Gong and Mr. Gao Ying have disagreements. However, it is very inconvenient for me to participate in the matter on my own initiative in this current situation. Mr. Gong is still in this port and will not return to China this month. I think you know this. Mr. Gao Ying's letter has been received. I will try my best to inquire about the matters mentioned. Please inform and explain to Mr. Gao that I am not allowed to receive English letters because he is detained in the detention center. Please explain my duties and position to Mr. Gong, because you are also a lawyer and understand the etiquette that should be observed in the performance of duties.

Sincerely,

Lawyer Walter Lair

February 6, 1930

Second Robbery of Zhangyan Town in Jinshan 78

Songjiang Telegram: The county government received a long-distance phone call from Tinglin last night (the 1st), reporting that over thirty bandit ships, carrying more than four hundred bandits armed with guns, had come to the neighboring town of Zhangyan. They passed through Songyin Town around 4-5 PM and headed straight for Zhangyan, towed by small steamers. Gunfire could now be faintly heard in Tinglin, which is only eighteen miles from Zhangyan, making the situation very critical. In addition to sending detectives in separate groups to investigate, the Public Security Bureau had first sent an urgent report, and so on. At the same time, the Water Police Department also received the same telegram from Liu Zigao, the leader of the first squad stationed in Zhu. It is found that Zhangyan is the leading town of Jinshan County with prosperous commerce. It was once robbed by bandits last October, with losses of tens of thousands of yuan. Later, its defense capabilities were strengthened, and security guards and firearms were added. Unexpectedly, not long after, it suffered a second robbery disaster, which is truly shocking. According to inquiries from various sources, the gang of bandits numbered over four hundred, divided into thirty-six boats. First, they seized a small steamer at the entrance of the Cuanlai Temple to tow them. When passing through Songyin Town at about 4 PM, the townspeople knew something was wrong when they saw a large number of tugboats. After the bandit boats passed, they telegraphed Tinglin to be on guard. Some bandits had already been lurking in Zhangyan, first spreading rumors to create a terrifying atmosphere. In the evening, a large group of bandits went ashore to seize weapons from the Public Security Bureau. The security guards and police officers immediately went on duty to resist, but due to their numerical disadvantage, two guards and police officers were killed, and three were injured. Most of the firearms were seized. The shops in the town did not have time to close their doors and had to let the bandits search and plunder. Li Xinglin, a clerk of a pawnshop, was kidnapped by the bandits. Anyone with a little wealth was kidnapped, but the number of people taken is unknown. Only Mr. Yao Shizi was talking on the phone with Songjiang. As soon as he hung up the receiver, he heard gunfire everywhere. Knowing that something had happened, he sneaked out the back door and hid in the countryside, fortunately avoiding being kidnapped. At the same time, more than fifty students, both male and female, from Liuxi Elementary School were all kidnapped. During the fierce fighting between the police and the bandits, bullets were flying everywhere, and many civilians were injured. The looting ended at 11 PM. A bandit who seemed to be the leader blew a whistle to gather the team and get on the boat, and forced the Shanghai-Zhangyan passenger ship to tow them. The bandits carried the stolen goods and escorted the hostages, one after another, getting off the boat all the way. They looked very calm, carrying the loot and the hostages down the boat. It is said that they left via Zhangjing and passed through the No. 34 railway bridge, probably using Mao Lake as their destination. Zhang Yunfeng, the first district inspector of the Provincial Water Police Force, is currently leading shallow-water warships to pursue them. The whereabouts of all the hijacked boats and hostages are unknown, and the losses are feared to be greater than the first robbery last year. Today, the shops in the town are said to be closed. The citizens are uneasy because some of them have been kidnapped. The situation is filled with sorrow and disaster, and the aftermath is feared to be difficult to handle. Except for guarding the key passes, most of the troops under He Yalin of the Water Police have been ordered to gather in Jinze and other places to join forces with the second, third, and fourth divisions to encircle and suppress the bandit gang of Taibao Ashu. Therefore, there were no water police stationed in Zhangyan. Captain He himself was in Shanghai for medical treatment yesterday. Special Article 94

China Gradually Adopts the Gold Standard

Summary of the Draft Currency Law (Continued)

Gradual Adoption of the Gold Standard

The draft stipulates that the gold standard should be gradually implemented in various provinces. The first step is to announce the date of the gold standard currency system in one or several provinces. After that, the new currency will gradually become legal tender, and it can be used for wages, deposits, and any other transactions. Unless otherwise stipulated by the Minister of Finance, the government will also use it for receipts and payments at the rate of one Sun equal to one yuan. New currency exchange offices will be set up in various convenient places so that people can exchange old currency for new currency at the rate set by the Minister of Finance. This official rate may vary from province to province and can be changed at any time. Within one year from the aforementioned date, the second date, the so-called Gold Standard Legal Tender Date, will be announced. After that, only gold standard currency will become legal tender for concluding contracts. The second date shall not be less than one year after the first date and shall be announced at least six months before implementation. The third date is the Debt Conversion Date. This date may be the same as or different from the Legal Tender Date, but it shall not be before the Legal Tender Date, and its implementation shall be at least six months after the announcement. After that, all payments of debts calculated in other non-gold standard currencies shall be paid at the expiration date at the exchange rate of new and old currencies originally stipulated for this purpose. These debt conversion rates are based on the market price of each currency in the 90 days before the announcement of the conversion date. Once determined, it will be used as an example forever. The current copper coins are temporarily accommodated by the gold standard. The draft stipulates that the current ten-wen or one-fen copper coins will continue to be used temporarily and accommodated by the gold standard. The circulation rate of these currencies varies from place to place, and about 300 copper coins can often be exchanged for one silver dollar. The draft stipulates that the circulation of ten-wen copper coins should be reduced to 200 coins per Sun. After this is successful, the Copper Coin Consolidation Date will be announced. After that, copper coins will become a legitimate part of the gold standard, and their redemption will be at a rate of one-half fen per coin or 200 coins per Sun. The copper content of the current ten-wen copper coins is higher than their face value, and private individuals melt the copper coins to extract the copper they contain. Therefore, it is beneficial for the government to recover these excessive copper coins. When the circulation of copper coins is reduced from 300 coins per Sun to 200 coins per Sun, their face value has increased. Unless the price of copper is higher than it is today, profiteers will not be able to melt them for profit. Making the current ten-wen copper coins accommodate the gold standard will greatly help the adoption and circulation of the gold standard, because it can make people know that one Sun coin actually represents 200 copper coins, a five-fen nickel coin represents 10 copper coins, or a one-jiao nickel coin represents 20 copper coins. Nickel coins will become a necessity for small transactions, so the government can have huge minting profits. After the old copper coins are consolidated, they will be gradually replaced by small half-fen new copper coins (to be continued).

Then he delivered a speech, representing the National Government to express sincere welcome. This participation is by outstanding and strong revolutionary youths from all over the country. The impact is hoped to have a great contribution to the national people. At present, feudal ideology is still prevalent in the country, hindering the Three People's Principles and the National Revolution. Athletes are urged to bring Premier Sun's principles back to their local areas to promote them, so that residual warlords and feudal ideas will no longer exist, in order to seek freedom and equality and achieve the spirit of national independence. Then, Lu Ming, a representative from Shanghai, signed a speech, hoping to promote national sports and children's physical education with the government's power under Chairman Jiang's leadership. The representative from Liaoning said that they could not take the Chinese train from Tianjin and had to take a Japanese ship from Dalian, which made them feel infinite emotion, and relayed the instructions of Commander Zhang upon their departure and the aspirations of the people of Liaoning Province. The representative from Harbin requested to promote sports to enhance international status, it is said.

Preliminary Round, Second Day, Liaoning Wins Against Zhejiang 116

The result was two to one. The competition was very fierce. The Liaoning football team is mostly composed of famous players from Fengyong University and Northeastern University. They have a good reputation in North China. This time, representing Liaoning to fight in the south, their strength cannot be underestimated. The team leader, Feng Yong, is also very attentive, so this trip has great hopes. Zhejiang's strength is also considered not weak. Yesterday afternoon at 1 pm, the two teams fought at the football field. The competition was very fierce. As a result, Liaoning won with two to one. Zhejiang's defeat was due to the ineffectiveness of the defense. The forward Liu Zongde performed the best. Goalkeeper Lu Shutian also had amazing performances from time to time. Liaoning's forwards were brave, but their movements were too slow, and their shots were also long and accurate.

(1) Situation in the First Half 117

Under the referee Tang Zhongguang's mobilization order, the Zhejiang team kicked the ball to attack, and it was kicked out by the right back of the Liaoning team. After several passes, the ball approached the Zhejiang team's goal. Cai Sicheng of Liaoning shot, but it was blocked. Unexpectedly, one wave subsided, and another wave rose. Liaoning pressed in with great momentum again. The left inside forward dribbled the ball and shot, and the Zhejiang goalkeeper Lu Shutian showed his skills again. After the Zhejiang team escaped danger, the forwards became lively. The Liaoning side became busy. Once the Zhejiang Guangdong Football Team Lin Zemin Photo

The Zhejiang team's left inside forward dribbled straight up, as if entering an uninhabited area. Just as he was thinking of attacking, he was suddenly snatched by the Liaoning right back and passed to center forward Cai Sicheng. Then the Liaoning team's forwards were like wolves and tigers, directly approaching the Zhejiang goal. Right wing Hui Rongzhang penetrated deep into the enemy's formation and sent the ball to the center. Liu Baochen caught up and kicked it in, opening the scoring. The score was one to zero in the first half.

(2) Situation in the Second Half 118

Changing sides to fight again, the Zhejiang team bravely advanced, trying to recover. Sure enough, God fulfilled their wishes. The Zhejiang team got a free kick opportunity, led by the center back, kicking the right wing and getting the ball in the middle. The center forward got a chance to shoot and scored a goal, creating a situation where each side had one goal. Then the Liaoning team raised their arms and shouted, and the momentum of the ball changed. At that time, the ball hovered in front of the Zhejiang team's goal for about five or six minutes. The Zhejiang team had difficulty coping. Soon, the Liaoning team's left inside forward scored again. Afterwards, both sides showed signs of fatigue, and until the end, neither side gained anything. The score was one to one in the second half. The overall result was two to one, with Liaoning winning. Referee Tang Zhongguang, linesmen Shen Huichun and Chen Jixiang.

Women's Basketball 124

Preliminary Round Jiangsu Wins Big Against Anhui

37 to 7 Today (2nd), the women's basketball game began at 10 a.m. The competitors were Jiangsu and Anhui. Both teams were the elite of their provinces, and their strengths were similar. It was expected that the competition would be fierce, so the spectators were enthusiastic. Minister of Foreign Affairs Wang Zhengting also came to the venue to watch.

Jiangsu Wins in the First Half 125

After the game started, Jiangsu immediately pounced on the enemy. The connection between the forwards was quite good, but because it was their first appearance, they inevitably made some mistakes, and their shots were not accurate. Soon, Sun Shuquan of Jiangsu received a pass from Zhang Yingfen and opened the scoring. Anhui tried its best to resist, and Yang Zhuangmei also made a free throw, making the score 2 to 1, which ended the first quarter. In the second quarter, Jiangsu exerted great pressure, and the connection between the forwards was even better. The shots were also gradually accurate, so they scored more points.

Jiangsu Finishes Smoothly in the Second Half 126

The Su team replaced all the guards with substitutes, and Anhui gained a slight advantage. In the fourth quarter, Jiangsu regained its prestige and momentum, and center Sun Shuquan was extremely brave, charging and cooperating with Zhang Mao and others, repeatedly scoring, and scoring 19 points alone. Anhui lacked training in shooting. Yang Zhuangmei had 15 free throw opportunities, but only scored 2 points, otherwise it might have been saved in the event of a worst-case scenario. The result was 37 to 7, Jiangsu won completely. The scores of each quarter were 3 to 1, 17 to 3, 4 to 2, and 14 to 1, all of which were advantageous for Jiangsu. Referee Shao Ji, inspector Zhang Huilan.

Sports Advancement Association Discussion 135

Attending the Far Eastern Games

Organizing Various Selection Committees. Track and Field, Tennis: Individuals as the Standard. Basketball: Winners as the Basis. Baseball: Pending the Arrival of the Honolulu Team.

The Sports Advancement Association's Wang Zhengting and Hao Boyang, at 10 PM on the 2nd, invited representatives from various individual associations to hold an important meeting. More than twenty people attended, with Ma Yuehan as chairman. They discussed the selection of Chinese representatives to participate in the upcoming Far Eastern Games. It was resolved to organize various selection committees: Track and Field (7 people), Chairman Hao Gengsheng, Committee members Qiu Jixiang, Gao Xiwei, Zhang Xinfu, Jiang Xiangqing, Ma Yuehan, Zhang Jiwu; Swimming (3 people), Chairman Zhang Wucheng, Committee members Lin Xitao, Tang Fuxiang; Soccer (3 people), Chairman Tang Fuxiang, Committee members Yu Hengzhi; Basketball (5 people), Chairman Dong Shouyi, Committee members Xu Zhendong, Ma Yuehan, Lu Songen, Wei Zesheng; Volleyball (3 people), Chairman Xu Minhui, Committee members Qiu Jixiang, Gao Zhuiwei; Baseball (3 people), Chairman Liu Dacheng, Committee members Zhang Guoxun, Shen Weichang; Tennis (1 person), Hao Boyang.

Women's selection issue, presided over by Hao Boyang. It was also resolved that the selection criteria for each event would be as follows: Track and field and swimming would be based on individual results. Soccer teams would be formed by combining players. Basketball and volleyball would be based on the national championship teams, with additional outstanding players selected. Baseball would be decided after the Honolulu team arrives. Tennis would be based on individual results. The issue of amateur qualifications was discussed at the end. Today's competition schedule:

General Review of the Two-Day Track and Field Competition 138

Day Two: Liu Changchun injured his foot, no outstanding performance. Female hero Sun Guiyun moves as if flying.

In the track and field competition on the first day, short-distance prodigy Liu Changchun, except for the 200 meters, had no good results, which greatly disappointed the audience. According to Xiao Dinghua, Liu injured his hamstring severely during training in Shanghai. Fortunately, he received prompt treatment, but it has not fully healed. It is believed that he may recover by the time he goes to the Far East Games. Liu's start in the 100 meters was extremely slow, and he did not exert himself until after 30 meters, hence the poor result. However, Zhou Zhaoyuan and Zhong Lianji worked very hard, and it is expected that the 100-meter final will see fierce competition between Liu, Zhou, and Zhong. In the 400 meters, Liu seemed to deliberately concede, frequently looking back as he approached the finish line, resulting in second place. Liu was very diligent in the 200 meters (Lin Zemin Photo), although the time was quite different than Xiao's previous record of 22.2 seconds, it was still a leading result in the day's events. In the women's track events, the East Special District's results seem to be the best. Female hero Sun Guiyun moves as if flying. At the sound of the gun, the yellow uniform dazzled the eyes, maintaining a distance of more than ten steps from the second-place runner. After the race, she was surrounded by photographers and received a burst of applause.

Wang Yuan's performance was also not bad. There is no doubt that the East Special District will win the track and field championship. Sun is still young, has excellent form, and with diligent training, it will not be difficult to become an international athlete. There were no remarkable results in the high and low hurdles races. In the 1500 meters, the northeastern talents showed their prowess again. Zhao Dexin and Jiang Yunlong secured the first and second positions, respectively, with a "who else but me" attitude in the final. The high jump final was one of the most exciting scenes of yesterday. More than fifty people participated. At 1.689 meters, only Tianjin's Li Zhongsan, Liaoning's Fu Baorui, Beiping's Wu Yunlong, and Shanghai's Su Zuxie jumped over. The rest failed three times. It was especially regrettable that Fu's hand knocked the bar down each time. Shanghai's Su was also able to cope with effort. As a result, the three tied for second place. Then Li jumped over once again, with a height of 1.73 meters, which is still far from the national record. He should practice diligently, otherwise we may not have a place in the Far East Games. In the women's shot put final, the result was 7.845 meters. The national record is 8.33 meters, held by Chen Xinyuan. Unfortunately, Chen was eliminated yesterday due to poor spirits. It is hoped that Chen will strive harder in the coming sessions and regain the championship. Day Two. Men's 100 meters: In yesterday's men's 100-meter semi-finals, short-distance athletes Liu Changchun, Zhong Lianji, and Jiang Peng all took first place. Liu's result was slightly better than the previous day, but his start was still very slow, lagging behind especially around 50 meters. When he reached the finish line, he sprinted hard and surpassed Hao Chunde. Shanghai's Jiang Peng had a very good result in yesterday's race. The famous North China general Zhou Zhaoyuan even retreated to second place. It is expected that there will be fierce competition between Shanghai and Liaoning in the 100-meter final. If Liu Changchun does not achieve a time of within 11 seconds, Zhong and Jiang may compete with him for the top spot.

Men's 200 meters: In the men's 200-meter semi-final, Zhou Ende led at the start of the first group. Liu Changchun's start was still very slow. At around 250 meters, Liu was in second place, swinging his arms and looking up as he chased hard. Unexpectedly, he still won first place at the finish line, which was not easy. However, the result was really not good. In the second group, Tianjin's Zhou Zhaoyuan started before Zhong Lianji, and Zhong also caught up at the finish line. In the final, the two heroes from the north and the south will meet. It is unknown who will win. Men's 800 meters: The results of yesterday's 800-meter heats were not very outstanding. In the first lap of the first group, Liaoning's Lang Dakui and Pang Shirong took the first and second positions in turn. Unexpectedly, in the last half-lap, Jiangsu's Song Ze'an snatched the lead, which was quite surprising. In the second group, Liaoning's Xue Yuxiang also took the lead at the start. Shanghai's Deng Zhiming caught up in the second lap. Although Xue tried hard to chase, he was unable to catch up. It is expected that Liaoning will have difficulty winning the final if they do not make a special effort. Women's 50 meters: In yesterday's women's 50-meter semi-final, Sun Guiyun of the East Special District maintained her original speed and won first place in the first group. In the second group, Wang Yuan, a famous player from the East Special District, started too quickly and committed two fouls. The third time, she inevitably felt apprehensive. She dared to start racing only after the gun was fired and tried hard to catch up, but the distance was too great, and she was unable to recover, which was a great pity. Men's High Hurdles: In yesterday's high hurdles semi-final, Liaoning's Ding Hua maintained the first position. Shanghai's Cao Yu started slower and gradually caught up in the middle section, finishing third. At the start of the second group, Beiping's Wang Yuzhen moved as if flying and took the lead immediately. He broke through past Fujian's Lin Shaozhou at 80 meters and was several steps ahead of Lin at the finish line, showing great promise in the final.

Men's 400 meters: In yesterday's 400-meter semi-final, short-distance prodigy Liu Changchun maintained first place in the second group, but the result was still not good. Guangdong's Mai Guozhen, who took first place in the first group, had a decent result and will compete with Shanghai's Zhu Ruihong for the runner-up spot in the final. Shot Put

In the final of the twelve-pound shot put, 22 athletes competed, but there were no good results. They were all average. Liaoning's Fan Guangwu's third throw reached 13.115 meters. Shanghai's shot put expert Dai Ming achieved 13.10 meters in the second attempt. The rest were all within 13 meters. With the third throw, Dai Ming jumped to the top spot with 13.30 meters. Unexpectedly, Shanghai's Pan Nanshun pushed hard with the sixth throw and won first place with 13.34 meters. Although the result was slightly different from the national record of 14.11 meters, it was far from the Far Eastern record of 14.23 meters. It is hoped that they will work harder so that there is hope.

Women's Baseball Throwing Competition 139

The women's baseball throwing final was the best result of yesterday and the focus of the entire venue. Talents gathered, and the differences were extremely small. There were seven or eight people who threw over 33 meters. Guangdong's Chen Peitao threw 38.46 meters in the first throw, and the entire venue applauded. With a swing of her jade arm, the ball flew like an arrow, which was astounding. Second place went to Hunan's Yang Ren, and third place went to Beiping's Hu Ruixiu. Their results were all over 34 meters. Shanghai's Fan Ruimei, who had a result of 38 meters, was eliminated, which was a great pity. Jump.

In the long jump final, Shanghai's Hao Chunde took the lead with 6.01 meters, but the result was not satisfactory. In the daily trials, he jumped more than six meters easily. However, Hao only achieved 6.01 meters to win first place. Guangdong's Situ Guang finished second with a difference of 0.01 meters. The field events seemed to be relatively poor overall, possibly due to the weather. It has been very cold for several days. If it is warmer, the results may be better. Compared to the national record of 6.74 meters and the Far Eastern record of 7.09 meters, the results this time are far behind.

Dai Jitao's Speech 140

Seeing the Significance of Sports from Chinese History and Culture

Dai Jitao, President of the National Games, came to Hangzhou this time to preside over the Games. Seeing the enthusiasm of athletes from all over the country and the progress of their physiques, he was very pleased. In addition to a sincere speech at the welcome meeting on the evening of the 1st, he also delivered an important speech, expounding the meaning of sports being connected to politics from the founding basis of China and the political philosophy of past dynasties. The following is a transcript of his speech.

In recent years, Chinese citizens have gradually realized the importance of sports. The National Games have been held three times, but this is considered the first time that the central government has initiated and presided over it. My opinion has already been written in the opening speech of the Games, but I still have some thoughts to share with everyone at this time. In recent years, in my study of ancient Chinese history, regarding the composition of the nation and the construction of the country, I have discovered a unique feature that other countries do not have, which is that both in political theory and in policy, sports are the foundation. Ancient history is not recorded in detail, making it quite difficult to know, but compared to other countries, the myths are unreasonable, and China is the best, and the general situation is also very correct. In the Fuxi era, China had writing. Shennong's civil administration and military achievements were both extremely far-reaching. The foundation of a unified national state was laid at this time. By the time of the Yellow Emperor, the composition of a great nation and the construction of a great country were completely successful. Therefore, many Chinese historians highly respect the Yellow Emperor as the first ancestor of the Chinese nation. The foundation of state-building in these two dynasties was very unique. Shennong was an inventor of medicine, and the Yellow Emperor was also a great scholar of medical hygiene. The Nei Jing, which is circulated today, may not be the work of the Yellow Emperor era, but it is certain that the Yellow Emperor's politics were based on medical hygiene as the foundation of all political theory and practice. Over the millennia, what has enabled the Chinese nation to become great is entirely due to this. I have not studied foreign history, but as far as I know, building a country with medicine and hygiene as the foundation of political theory and with medical hygiene as a specialized skill is certainly unprecedented in foreign history. Regarding the Hong Fan in the Book of Documents, whether it is true or not, scholars have different opinions, but what is recorded in this book is sufficient to explain the general political philosophy of the Three Dynasties, at least a kind of political philosophy that records the tradition of the Shang Dynasty, claiming that the purpose of politics is to enable the people to achieve five blessings and eliminate six extremes. The so-called five blessings are: first, longevity; second, wealth; third, health; fourth, love of virtue; fifth, a peaceful death. The six extremes are: first, violent death; second, disease; third, worry; fourth, poverty; fifth, evil; sixth, weakness. From this, it can be seen that the most important thing in the political proposals at that time was health and longevity for the people. Such political theories are indeed great, accurate, and unique to other countries, very practical and very important. Later generations explained the principles of self-cultivation and the methods of governing the country in an increasingly abstract way, and the meaning of morality almost turned into mythology, which is truly lamentable. Until modern times, our Chinese nation's teacher of revival, the founder of the Republic of China, Dr. Sun Yat-sen, was also a medical expert. In his theory of psychological construction, he said that all of human civilization is nothing more than returning to the two words "maintenance." Only by using the natural ability of self-cultivation to resist all diseases can one achieve health. I believe that all of the Premier's doctrines and policies come from this principle. Because I discovered these major events in history, and because I have personally suffered the pain of physical illness and the pain of illness hindering my career and work, I have become more aware of the importance of sports and hygiene. Indeed, all profound and great knowledge requires a strong body and mind to acquire and apply. As for the meaning of morality, I believe that the method of acquiring a strong body and spirit is the Dao, and being able to work hard and unremittingly and help others to do so is Virtue. The method of enabling a group to have a strong organization and doctrine is the Dao, and being able to work hard and unremittingly and help others and other groups to do so is Virtue. Therefore, the meaning of morality is simply connected to sports and hygiene, and sometimes it can even be used as an explanation. Especially the Taoists in China, who specialize in morality, completely regard sports and hygiene as the essence of all morality. Our Chinese nation has reached its extreme point of weakness. The biggest shortcoming is obviously that both body and spirit are weak. In foreign countries, whether it is a politician, a soldier, a scholar, or an industrialist, they are still in their prime at the age of fifty or sixty, and they are only considered old at the age of seventy or eighty. Originally, no matter what kind of career it is, one always has to reach the age of forty or fifty to learn, be able to create independently, and truly have the confidence to teach and the ability to lead. If one dies or declines at the age of forty or fifty, then one has achieved nothing. If a nation as a whole dies or declines at the age of forty or fifty, then the culture of this nation, no matter what, cannot be created. At this moment, to save the Chinese nation in construction, all kinds of careers are certainly important, but to save the essence of the Chinese nation, medicine and sports are two very important things. Medicine is still passive rescue and treatment, which is to save people who are already ill and declining. Only paying attention to sports is a positive and important way to create a strong body that cannot be invaded by all diseases, cannot be harmed by all poisons, and cannot be injured by strong enemies. With this foundation, whatever science or career can be learned well, and what has been learned can be brought into play. I myself am willing to work hard in this way, and I hope that all compatriots across the country will understand this meaning and strive to implement it. Whether it is a school or various groups, especially in various villages, it is necessary to recognize that sports is the only way to save oneself, save others, save the country, and save the world, and to promote it with all efforts. Then sports competitions are a method to achieve the above-mentioned goals, and it is definitely not the meaning of setting up a ring like in China. The reason why sports in China cannot progress is partly due to the savagery of setting up a ring. Therefore, we must know that for those who sincerely work hard and participate in various competitions, the winners and the losers are worthy of everyone's praise and worthy of everyone's commendation, and those who are less skilled and lose are also worthy of everyone's praise and worthy of everyone's respect. It is necessary to eliminate the thinking of setting up a ring in the feudal era, abide by the rules of sports, and respect the morality of sports. Only then can sports become popular and turn into a mass movement. I hope that all the representatives and athletes in various places will fully recognize this point and strive to promote it.

There are twenty in the women's dormitory and sixty in the men's dormitory, which is not enough to allocate because there are several times more male athletes than female athletes.

New Life on the Road 146

The Guangdong male and female athletes are staying at the West Lake Hotel on Hubin Road. The hotel is very elegant, with a large patio originally used for tourists to walk and rest. Now it is used by the male and female athletes as a training ground for playing ball. Every time the sun sets, those who are relaxing on Hubin Road and passing by the gate cannot help but stop to watch. The tourists upstairs and downstairs, reclining on the corridors and steps, with a cup of tea, gaze at the lake and mountains from afar and watch the ball game up close. With a happy mind and body, they feel as if they are in a fairyland. It is truly a blessing to travel.

Poor Food Barely Fills the Stomach 147

The General Assembly needs to open more than 300 tables for each meal. Therefore, the dishes that are cooked are difficult to swallow. The rice is either mushy or hard, and the dishes are either bland or salty. Therefore, athletes from all over the country have already expressed their dissatisfaction. Yesterday, three athletes from Tianjin had diarrhea all day long. It is said that it was also a gift from the food. There is no market around the General Assembly. However, since the problem of eating is necessary for everyone, there are many residents near the General Assembly who are running speculative meal packages and restaurants. Because the food inside the General Assembly is too bad, they would rather find food outside. Therefore, these temporary shops are doing very well.

The event drew a massive crowd. Besides the Boy Scouts maintaining order, police were stationed everywhere to keep order. Thanks are due to the Zhejiang police authorities for their enthusiasm. When he broke into the track and field arena, he lingered near the area where a certain girls' school was stationed. The monitors noticed him and ordered him to leave, but he refused. Then five or six policemen came and sternly told him to respect himself in uniform. Seeing that he was outnumbered, the soldier fled with his head in his hands.

National Boy Scout Grand Review 165

Held on the 18th of this month The Chinese Boy Scouts have been established for almost a year. Now, in order to examine the results of their past training, it has been decided to convene in Nanjing from the 18th of this month to hold the first grand review and practice various military drills. The headquarters of the army has notified the Boy Scouts in various places to arrive in Beijing on schedule. The various things heard are published as follows. Collection The first national general review and grand camping of the Chinese Boy Scouts was decided a month ago, and it will be held in Nanjing on April 18. Now that the deadline is approaching, the commander-in-chief's office has sent personnel to the Ministry of Communications to discuss free travel for Boy Scouts to and from various places. Minister Wang Boqun of the Ministry of Communications agreed. Now it has been presented to the Ministry, saying that the significance of this national Boy Scout review is to assess the results of the year and make universal improvements in the future, so that the young children of the whole country can be trained to truly believe in the Three Principles of the People and be successors to the national revolution. It is an unprecedented initiative and a special situation, not other matters of regret that can be used as precedents. Considering that all countries in the world provide free travel on trains and ships for Boy Scouts traveling domestically on weekdays.

The Boy Scouts have been issued a specific free pass by the commander-in-chief's office, which is valid until the 18th of this month, and they must gather in the capital. Command This grand review and camping will all refer to the current military actions of the army system, so the post of commander-in-chief has been publicly recommended to be taken by He Yingqin. From the 18th, the Boy Scouts' exercises and drill codes will all be under the command of He. Free The Ministry of Communications has notified all railway bureaus and shipping companies that from April 4th, Boy Scouts from various places who come to the capital for review will be exempt from fares. All free passes and rules for taking trains have been ordered by the headquarters, and five copies will be issued with each, specifying the validity period from April 4th to May 5th, after which they will no longer be valid. All roads have followed suit, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, with more routes, has also been notified to comply. The bureau has forwarded the free pass samples to various ships for reference yesterday.

The Ministry of Education Approves the Flexible Measures for Examining and Approving Textbooks 166

The Ministry of Education, according to the difficulties reported by the Zhonghua Book Company in deleting the general title, requested approval for flexible measures, and submitted sample pages of the New Zhonghua New Primary School Chinese Language Reader for approval. All departments have now approved it and ordered the education administrative organs of all provinces and cities to instruct all bookstores to comply. The previous regulations of the Ministry regarding the matters to be marked on the cover of various textbooks, including six consolidation measures, and the deletion of general titles such as New Era and New Doctrine, have been issued to all bookstores for compliance and correction. Subsequently, the Shanghai Bookstore Association submitted a statement stating that the deletion of the general title was difficult and requested appropriate flexible measures. The Ministry rejected this and reiterated the previous order to all bookstores for compliance and not to delay in the slightest. Now, the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company has reported that the cancellation of the words "New Zhonghua" and "New Primary School" will make it easy for the names of various bookstores to be confused, and it will be difficult for purchasers to identify them. They requested a review and instructions for compliance and attached two sample pages of the New Zhonghua Chinese Language Reader and the New Primary School Chinese Language Reader. The Ministry previously stated that the various textbooks published by various bookstores often have the same specific general title above the names of the various books, as a set. The name is cumbersome, and it is doubtful whether the editing has a complete plan and whether the content has a clear and practical connection. Moreover, the quality of teaching materials varies, and some books in the same set have been approved by the Ministry, while others have not. Therefore, although the name is a set, many are incomplete. The specific general title that makes up a set has long lost its effect, so it has been repeatedly ordered to be deleted to be consistent with the name. Now, the bookstore has repeatedly reported the difficulties of the bookstore and purchasers, and has changed the New Zhonghua Textbook and New Primary School Textbook to the three words "New Zhonghua New Primary School", which are listed at the top of the book name and combined into one line. The name "Textbook" has been changed to "Textbook", called "New Zhonghua XX Textbook" and "New Primary School XX Textbook". The name is relatively simple and easy to identify. It is also reasonable that it is easy to confuse in each bureau and that purchasers have difficulty in identifying each situation. A temporary flexible measure is allowed. The New Zhonghua Chinese Language Textbook and New Primary School Chinese Language Textbook names submitted by the Association should be approved for adoption. However, the names of subsequent textbooks should be simplified as much as possible to be clear and appropriate, and submitted to the Ministry for approval at any time to achieve uniformity. In addition to *

The instructions should be issued again, and all bookstores should be instructed to comply.

Chairman Chiang's Actions After Arriving in Shanghai 167

Yesterday Spoke to Officers of the Fifth Division Met with Important Figures Such as Yu Youren Chiang is Scheduled to Return to Beijing from Hangzhou Today or Tomorrow After Chairman Chiang and his wife arrived at the Xinlonghua Railway Station by special train, they stayed in the train overnight because it was midnight. At dawn yesterday morning, they left Xinlonghua and arrived at the North Railway Station at 7:00 a.m. Mr. and Mrs. Chiang got out of the car and took a car to the Song Residence on Seymour Road. At 3:30 p.m., Mr. Chiang went to Longhua and summoned Commander Xiong of the Fifth Division and Zhou Regiment Commander of the Sixth Regiment, Xu Regiment Commander of the Twenty-seventh Regiment, and Xiao Regiment Commander of the Twenty-ninth Regiment, as well as officers such as battalion commanders, platoon commanders, and company commanders, to speak at the auditorium of the Songhu Garrison Command. All officers above the section chief of the Garrison Command also participated, a total of about 300 people. Mr. Chiang spoke for an hour, mainly about believing in the Three Principles of the People, sharing weal and woe with soldiers, clear rewards and punishments, and combining leniency and strictness to encourage the officers. Mr. Chiang then extended his greetings to Shao Lizi, Yu Youren, Zhang Qun, Chen Guangfu, Yin Rugeng, Yu Qiaqing, Chen Shaokuan, Xiong Shihui and others at the Song Residence on Seymour Road at about 5:00 p.m. Qian Xinzhi was also supposed to be on the list of those summoned yesterday, but because Qian happened to return to his hometown to sweep the tombs, it was postponed to another meeting. Chiang is scheduled to return to Beijing today or tomorrow.

Rice Arrives in Sufficient Quantities 168

Rice Merchants Secretly Control

Wuchen Society reported that the Social Affairs Bureau received reports that, during this tense rice market,*

Some rice merchants and boat owners who sell rice are watching the situation and hoping to raise prices, which is of great concern. Yesterday, they sent personnel to both the north and south markets to find out that the rice boats arriving at the port were still enthusiastic and had greatly increased compared with a few days ago. In this situation, the rice market should ease. However, most of the rice boats that arrived are stored under the river and not sold. The rice market is seeing a profit, but it has not been relaxed, and they are trying to make huge profits. According to yesterday's investigation, the number of rice boats arriving and stored unsold under the north and south markets is staggering. The list is as follows: It was also found that most of the rice boats that arrived in the north market were not sold. Some of the rice loaded on March 17 still had 60 stones that have not been

The Social Affairs Bureau plans to order the sale together with the Public Security Bureau. If anyone dares to violate the regulations, they will be punished.
